### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: There currently does not exist a Living Rules Reference section regarding The Fracture.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The Fracture consists of additional systems beyond the regular bounds of the game map.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: When a player gains their breakthrough, they roll a dice. On a result of 1 or 10, The Fracture enters play. Other game effects may also bring The Fracture into play.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: When The Fracture enters play, it is placed against the edge of the regular game map.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: When The Fracture is brought into play, neutral units are placed on the planets in The Fracture as well as the space area of those planets’ systems, as indicated on the reverse side of The Fracture tiles.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: When The Fracture is brought into play, several ingress tokens will be placed on the game board. Several systems in The Fracture contain a printed egress. Each ingress is adjacent to each egress, and vice versa. An ingress is not adjacent to an ingress and an egress is not adjacent to an egress.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If The Fracture was brought into play as a result of a player rolling a dice upon gaining their breakthrough, they will place ingress tokens according to the synergy on their breakthrough. For each color of technology in their breakthrough’s synergy, they choose three planets with a matching technology specialty, and place an ingress token in that planet’s system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If a different game effect places The Fracture into play, or The Fracture enters play because of the Nekro player’s breakthrough (which does not have a synergy), then the player that caused The Fracture to enter play chooses one planet with a technology specialty for each of the four colors of technology, and places ingress tokens in each of those planets’ systems.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If one system contains two planets with a technology specialty, only one of those planets may be chosen when placing ingress tokens.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: After ingress tokens are placed with either of these two methods, one additional ingress token is placed. If Thunder’s Edge is on the game board, then an ingress token is place into its system. Otherwise, an ingress token is placed into the Mecatol Rex system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A system cannot contain two or more ingress tokens.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: When a player gains control of a planet in The Fracture that is not already controlled by another player, they draw one relic card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Breakthroughs
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Neutral Units
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Relics
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Fracture
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Synergy
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A space dock is a structure that allows players to produce units.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each space dock has aProductionability that indicates the number of units it can produce.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: The primary way in which players acquire space docks is by resolving either the primary or secondary abilities of theConstructionstrategy card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Space docks are placed on planets. Each planet can have a maximum ofonespace dock.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If a player’s space dock is ever on a planet that does not contain any of their ground forces and contains a unit that belongs to another player, that space dock is destroyed.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A Space Dock is both a structure and a unit.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Space Dock
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Fighters transported during movement remain assigned to the transporting ship until movement is complete. They cannot be counted towards a space dock’s allocation until after movement is complete.
##################################################

--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Mechs are unique, faction–specific heavy ground forces.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Mechs are a type of ground force and can be transported and participate in ground combat.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each player begins with their mech unit card in play on their leader sheet and can produce mechs for the cost presented on the card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Some mechs haveDeployabilities which allow a player to place them on the game board without producing them normally.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Mech unit cards are not technologies.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Effects that refer to “ground forces” apply to mechs. Effects that refer to “infantry” do not.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: For notes about a mech of a specific faction, see that faction’s page.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Mechs
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Deploy

--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Units
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Opponent
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: During combat, a player’s opponent is the other player that either has ships in the system at the start of the space combat or has ground forces on the planet at the start of a ground combat.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Opponent
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Players who do not have units on either side of a combat are not opponents. Those players cannot use abilities or have abilities used against them that are used against an opponent.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Opponent
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Attacker

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A ship is a unit type consisting of carriers, cruisers, dreadnoughts, destroyers, fighters, and war suns. Each race also has a unique flagship.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Ships are always placed in space.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player can have a number of ships in a system equal to or less than the number of command tokens in that player’s fleet pool.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Ships can have any number of the following attributes: cost, combat, move, and capacity. These attributes are shown on faction sheets and unit upgrade technology cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A Fighter II may count towards either the fleet pool limit or a player’s capacity.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Capacity
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships

--- CONTENT: Combat
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Cost
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Fleet Pool
##################################################

--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics

--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics

### RULE_SOURCE: Ships
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Units
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Players can score objectives to gain victory points.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: There are two types of objective cards: public objectives and secret objectives.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each objective card indicates a number of victory points that a player gains by scoring that objective.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each objective card indicates the phase during which a player can score that objective – the status, action, or agenda phases.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each objective card describes the requirement a player must fulfill to score that objective.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If a player fulfills the requirement described on an objective card, they can score that objective following the timing indicated on the card, either during the action phase or the status phase.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player can score a maximum of one public objective and one secret objective during each status phase.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player can score any number of objectives during the agenda phase or during a turn of the action phase; however, they can only score one objective during or after each combat.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player can score each objective only once during the game.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If an objective requires a player to destroy one or more units, those units can be destroyed by producing hits against them, playing action cards, using technology, or any number of other abilities that use the “destroy” terminology.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Players can score some objectives by spending resources, influence, or tokens, as described by the objective card. To score such an objective, a player must pay the specified cost at the time indicated on the card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When scoring a public objective, the player places one of their control tokens on that objective’s card. Then, that player advances their control token on the victory point track a number of spaces equal to the number of victory points gained.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each game contains five stage I and five stage II public objective cards that the speaker places facedown near the victory point track during setup.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: During each status phase, the speaker reveals a facedown public objective card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If the speaker must reveal a facedown public objective card but all public objective cards are already revealed, the game ends immediately.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player cannot score public objectives if that player does not control each planet in their home system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When scoring a secret objective, a player reveals the objective by placing it faceup in their play area. Then, they place one of their control tokens on that objective’s card and advances their control token on the victory point track a number of spaces equal to the number of victory points gained.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player can only score their own secret objectives; a player cannot score secret objectives revealed by other players.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each player begins the game with one secret objective.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each player can have up tothree totalscored and unscored secret objectives.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player can gain secret objectives by resolving either the primary or secondary ability of theImperialstrategy card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A status phase objective must have its condition met during the status phase; any activity during the action phase is irrelevant.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Any number of players may score a given public objective during the status phase. Players are not blocked from scoring an objective if another player earlier in initiative order scores it first, unless the earlier player achieved victory and ended the game by doing so.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The number of secret objective cards in a player’s hand is public information.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player may choose to reveal any or all of the secret objective cards in their hand, if they so choose.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If multiple ground combats happen on separate planets as part of a single invasion during one action, one secret objective may be scored during each.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: TheBombardmentandSpace Cannonsteps happen outside of combat; any number of secret objectives may be scored during those steps, and do not prevent another secret objective being scored during combat that turn.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player may score an action phase secret objective when they are not the active player.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player with three scored secret objectives may draw a fourth. However, they must immediately shuffle it into the secret objective deck.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: For notes about specific objective cards, see theobjective card component notes page.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Action Phase
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Agenda Phase
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Imperial
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Status Phase
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Objective Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Victory Points
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: During theGround Combatstep of an invasion, if the active player has ground forces on a planet that contains another player’s ground forces, those players resolve a ground combat on that planet. To resolve a ground combat, players perform the following steps:
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 1 – Roll Dice: Each player rolls one die for each ground force they have on the planet; this is a combat roll. If a unit’s combat roll produces a result that is equal to or greater than that unit’s combat value, that roll produces a hit.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 2 – Assign Hits: Each player in the combat must choose one of their own ground forces on the planet to be destroyed for each hit result their opponent produced.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: After assigning hits, if both players still have ground forces on the planet, players resolve a new combat round starting with theRoll Dicestep.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Ground combat ends when only one player (or neither player) has ground forces on the planet.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The “start of combat” and “start of combat round” windows occur before theRoll Dicestep.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The “end of combat” and “end of combat round” windows occur after theAssign Hitsstep.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If ground combat is to happen on multiple planets during a single invasion step, they will be resolved planet by planet, after theSpace Cannon Defensestep has been resolved on all planets and before theEstablish Controlstep is resolved on any planet. The active player chooses the order combats are fought in.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player may score up to one secret objective per ground combat. If there is combat on multiple planets, a player may score a secret objective in each.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player may use theSustain Damageability of a unit involved in a combat, usually a mech, to cancel a hit produced by their opponent.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: No player may retreat from a ground combat.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Ground Combat
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The “0” side of the d10 represents a result of 10.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Invasion is a step of the tactical action during which the active player can land ground forces on planets to gain control of those planets.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: To resolve an invasion, players perform the following steps:
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 1 – Bombardment: The active player may use theBombardmentability of any of their units in the active system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 2 – Commit Ground Forces: If the active player has ground forces in the space area of the active system, that player may commit any number of those ground forces to land on any of the planets in that system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 3 – Space Cannon Defense: If the active player commits any ground forces to a planet that contains units that have theSpace Cannonability, thoseSpace Cannonabilities can be used against the committed ground forces.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 4 – Ground Combat: If the active player has ground forces on a planet in the active system that contains another player’s ground forces, those players resolve a ground combat on that planet.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Step 5 – Establish Control: The active player gains control of each planet they committed ground forces to if that planet still contains at least one of their ground forces.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Units are considered to be on the planet for game effects from theCommit Ground Forcesstep onward.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If a player gains control of an uncontrolled planet during theEstablish Controlstep, they explore it.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If a player gains control of a legendary planet, they gain the legendary planet ability card in addition to the planet card. The ability card will not be exhausted if it was readied.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If Mecatol Rex has the custodians token on it, a player must remove it before they may commit ground forces to it.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Invasion
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Active Player

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: The custodians token begins each game on Mecatol Rex. The token represents the caretakers that safeguard the seat of the empire until such time as the galactic council can be reconvened.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Units can move into the system that contains Mecatol Rex following normal rules; however, players cannot commit ground forces to land on Mecatol Rex until the custodians token is removed from the planet.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Before theCommit Ground Forcesstep of an invasion, the active player can remove the custodians token from Mecatol Rex by spending six influence. Then, that player must commit at least one ground force to land on the planet.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When a player removes the custodians token from Mecatol Rex, they take the token from the game board and place it in their play area. Then, they gain one victory point.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: After a player removes the custodians token from Mecatol Rex, the agenda phase is added to all subsequent game rounds, including the game round during which the custodians token was removed from Mecatol Rex.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The custodians token is not an attachment.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Agenda Phase
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Custodians Token
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Control
##################################################

--- CONTENT: Influence
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Distant Suns
--- CONTENT: If the Naaz–Rokha player has multiple Eidolon on the planet they explore, they will draw only one additional exploration card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Distant Suns
--- CONTENT: The Naaz–Rokha player must choose to use this ability before seeing the first exploration card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Distant Suns
--- CONTENT: If a planet has multiple traits, the additional exploration card must come from the same deck as the first.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Fabrication
--- CONTENT: If the relic deck is empty, the Naaz–Rokha player may still purge two relic fragments as an action.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Fabrication
--- CONTENT: If the Naaz–Rokha player has no command tokens in their reinforcements, they may still purge one relic fragment as an action.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Fabrication
--- CONTENT: Either or both of the relic fragments may beUnknown Relic Fragments.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Black Market Forgery(Promissory Note)
--- CONTENT: If there are no cards in the relic deck, a player cannot gain a relic. As such, a player cannot playBlack Market Forgerywhen the relic deck is empty.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Black Market Forgery(Promissory Note)
--- CONTENT: Either or both of the relic fragments may beUnknown Relic Fragments.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Pre–Fab Arcologies(Technology)
--- CONTENT: The planet is not readied until after the planet is explored. If theFreelancersexploration card is revealed, then:
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Supercharge(Technology)
--- CONTENT: Superchargedoes not modify anti–fighter barrage, bombardment or space cannon rolls.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Visz El Vir(Flagship)
--- CONTENT: Each mech will roll an additional die.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Visz El Vir(Flagship)
--- CONTENT: TheVisz El Virability applies to both Eidolon and Z–Grav Eidolon.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Hesh and Prit — Perfect Synthesis(Hero)
--- CONTENT: The Naaz–Rokha player may choose to perform the secondary ability of zero, one or two strategy cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Hesh and Prit — Perfect Synthesis(Hero)
--- CONTENT: The Naaz–Rokha player must choose which strategy cards they will perform the secondary abilities of before they resolve any of those abilities.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Hesh and Prit — Perfect Synthesis(Hero)
--- CONTENT: When resolving the abilities of two strategy cards, they may be resolved in either order. Game objects affected by the first strategy card ability may be affected by the second.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Hesh and Prit — Perfect Synthesis(Hero)
--- CONTENT: If a player is eliminated, the strategy cards that they had are considered “unchosen”.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Hesh and Prit — Perfect Synthesis(Hero)
--- CONTENT: If the Naaz–Rokha player has no command tokens in their reinforcements, they must use a command token from their command sheet when performing the secondary ability of the strategy cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Hesh and Prit — Perfect Synthesis(Hero)
--- CONTENT: If the Naaz–Rokha player has the Muaat player’sAlliancepromissory note, they will not gain a trade good from it when they use theirPerfect Synthesisability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon /Z–Grav Eidolon(Mech)
--- CONTENT: The Naaz–Rokha mechs are only Z–Grav Eidolon during theSpace Combatstep, only in the active system, and only in the space area.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon /Z–Grav Eidolon(Mech)
--- CONTENT: If the Naaz–Rokha player had an Eidolon in the space area of the active system, they must mandatorily use its ability to convert it to a Z–Grav Eidolon.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon /Z–Grav Eidolon(Mech)
--- CONTENT: Any effect that may target ships or non–fighter ships may target a Z–Grav Eidolon.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon /Z–Grav Eidolon(Mech)
--- CONTENT: A Z–Grav Eidolon is still a ground force and a mech.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon /Z–Grav Eidolon(Mech)
--- CONTENT: A Z–Grav Eidolon participating in a space combat may count towards scoring theDemonstrate Your Powersecret objective.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon /Z–Grav Eidolon(Mech)
--- CONTENT: When a Z–Grav Eidolon reverts back to an Eidolon at the end of combat, it will count towards capacity in the active system. Capacity limits must be met before proceeding to theInvasionstep.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Absolute Synergy(Breakthrough)
--- CONTENT: The four mechs can be anywhere in the same system; they need not be all on the same planet, and some or all may be in the space area.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Absolute Synergy(Breakthrough)
--- CONTENT: The mechs may be removed and the card flipped as soon as the four mechs are in the same system. For example, this may be done before space combat starts.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon Maximum(Mech)
--- CONTENT: When in the space area of a system, the Eidolon Maximum counts towards either of the Naaz–Rokha player’s capacity or fleet pool in that system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon Maximum(Mech)
--- CONTENT: If hits are produced by unit abilities against a group of the Naaz–Rokha player’s units that includes the Eidolon Maximum, then these hits must be assigned to the other eligible units in that group, if possible.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon Maximum(Mech)
--- CONTENT: The Eidolon Maximum only repairs during combats that it is participating in.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon Maximum(Mech)
--- CONTENT: The Naaz–Rokha player can never have two or more Eidolon Maximums on the game board.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon Maximum(Mech)
--- CONTENT: The Eidolon Maximum is considered a mech for all relevant game effects, such as rolling an additional dice from the effect of theVisz El Vir.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Naaz–Rokha Alliance
--- SECTION_ID: Eidolon Maximum(Mech)
--- CONTENT: The Eidolon Maximum is considered a ship for all relevant game effects.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Cards and faction sheets each have abilities that players can resolve to trigger various game effects.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If information in this Rules Reference contradicts the Learn to Play booklet, the Rules Reference takes precedence.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If a card ability contradicts information in the Rules Reference, the card takes precedence. If both the card and the rules can be followed at the same time, they should be.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each ability describes when and how a player can resolve it.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If a card has multiple abilities, each ability is presented as its own paragraph.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If an ability contains the word “Action” a player must use a component action during the action phase to resolve that ability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If an ability uses the word “cannot”, that effect is absolute.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When a player resolves an ability, they must resolve the ability in its entirety. Any parts of the ability preceded by the word “may” are optional, and the player resolving the ability may choose not to resolve those parts.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Abilities on components that remain in play are mandatory unless those abilities use the word “may”.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If an ability has multiple effects separated by the word “and”, a player must resolve as many of the ability’s effects as possible. However, if the player cannot resolve all of its effects, that player is allowed to resolve as many as they can.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Some abilities have a cost that is followed by an effect. The cost of an ability is separated from the effect by the word “to” or by a semicolon. A player cannot resolve the effect of such an ability if they cannot resolve that ability’s cost.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Some examples of an ability’s cost include spending resources, spending trade goods, spending command tokens, exhausting cards, purging cards, and activating specific systems.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If the timing of an ability uses the word “before” or “after”, the ability’s effect occurs immediately before or after the described timing event, respectively.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If the timing of an ability uses the word “when”, the ability’s effect occurs at the moment of the described timing event.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Effects that occur “when” an event happens take priority over effects that occur “after” an event happens.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If an ability uses the word “then”, a player must resolve the effect that occurs before the word “then” or they cannot resolve the effect that occurs after the word “then”.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each ability can be resolved once for each occurrence of that ability’s timing event. For example, if an ability is resolved “at the start of combat”, it can be resolved at the start of each combat.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If there are multiple abilities that players wish to resolve at the same time during theaction phase, each player takes a turn resolving an ability in initiative order, beginning with the active player. This process continues until each player has resolved each ability that they wish to resolve during that window.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If there are multiple abilities that players wish to resolve at the same time during thestrategyoragenda phases, players take turns resolving abilities starting with the speaker and proceeding clockwise. This process continues until each player has resolved each ability that they wish to resolve during that window.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: The opening paragraph of each ability found on an action card describes when a player can resolve that card’s ability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: The opening paragraph of most abilities found on promissory notes describes when a player can resolve that card’s ability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Abilities on agenda cards correspond to an outcome. Players resolve these abilities during the agenda phase after players vote for a particular outcome.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each faction has faction abilities presented on its faction sheet. Each faction’s flagship has one or more unique abilities. Some abilities provide players with perpetual effects.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Some units have unit abilities. These abilities are named and presented above a unit’s attributes on a player’s faction sheet or on a unit upgrade card. Each unit ability has unique rules for when a player can resolve that ability. The following abilities are unit abilities:
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If a unit’s ability uses the phrase “this system” or “this planet”, the ability is referring to the system or planet that contains that unit.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: An ability may be triggered during the timing window it was gained, if applicable. For example, if a player receives the Creuss player’sCreuss Iffpromissory note at the start of their turn, they may use it immediately.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: An ability from a single physical object cannot be resolved more than once in one timing window. For example, if a player starts their turn with the Creuss player’sCreuss Iffpromissory note in their hand (having received it on a previous turn) and uses it, they will not be able to use it a second time this turn, if they receive it again as part of a transaction.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Multiple action cards with the same name cannot be played during a single timing window to affect the same units or game effect. See theaction cards pagefor more details.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: During the action phase, abilities are resolved in the current relative turn order, starting with the active player. For example, if it is currently theTrade(5) player’s turn, they will have the option to resolve first, then theWarfare(6) player, then theTechnology(7) player, and so on.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The secondary abilities of strategy cards are resolved in clockwise order, after the primary ability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player may resolve “at the start of your turn” and “at the end of your turn” abilities on the turn that they pass.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: All abilities that occur “when” an event occurs all trigger before any abilities that occur “after” the same event occurs.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: All abilities that occur “after” an event occurs all trigger before any abilities that occur “before” the next event occurs.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Action Cards
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Active Player
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Initiative Order
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Leaders
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics

##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Relics
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Speaker
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities

##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Abilities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Technology
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Commodities represent goods that are plentiful for their own faction and are desired by other factions. A commodity has no inherent game effects, but converts into a trade good if given to or received from another player.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Commodities and trade goods are represented by opposite sides of the same token.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: The commodity value on a player’s faction sheet indicates the maximum number of commodities that player can have.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When an effect instructs a player to replenish commodities, that player takes the number of commodity tokens necessary so that the amount of commodities that player has equals the commodity value on their faction sheet. Then, those tokens are placed faceup in the commodity area of that player’s faction sheet.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When a player replenishes commodities, that player takes the commodity tokens from the supply.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Players can trade commodities following the rules for transactions. When a player receives a commodity from another player, the player who received that token converts it into a trade good by placing it in the trade good area of their command sheet with the trade good side faceup.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Any game effect that instructs a player to give a commodity to another player causes that commodity to be converted into a trade good.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player cannot spend commodities unless otherwise specified; a player can only trade them during a transaction.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Commodity tokens come in values of one and three. A player can swap between these tokens as necessary.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player starts the game with zero commodities.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If a player has their maximum number of commodities, and is instructed to replenish their commodities, they will take no commodities. However, they will still trigger any “when [this] player replenishes commodities” effects, most notably theTrade Agreementpromissory note.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Deals
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Trade
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Trade Goods
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Commodities
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Transactions
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Action cards provide players with various abilities that they can resolve as described on the cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each player draws one action card during each status phase.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Players can draw action cards by resolving the primary and secondary abilities of thePoliticsstrategy card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When a player draws an action card, they take the top card from the action card deck and add it to their hand of action cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Each player’s hand can have a maximum ofseven action cards. If a player ever has more than seven action cards, that player must choose seven cards to keep and discard the rest.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A player’s action cards remain hidden from other players until those cards are played.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: The first paragraph of each action card is presented in bold text and describes the timing of when that card’s ability can be resolved.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: To play an action card, a player reads and resolves the card’s ability text, making any decisions as prompted by the card. Then, that player discards the card, placing it in the action discard pile.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If an action card is canceled, that card has no effect and is discarded.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Players start the game with zero action cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: The number of action cards in a player’s hand is public information.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player may choose to reveal any or all of the action cards in their hand, if they so choose.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If the action card deck is depleted, immediately shuffle the discard pile to form a new action card deck.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: During the action phase, action cards are dealt out in initiative order.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If a player’s action card is cancelled, usually via aSabotageaction card, then if that player has a second copy of that action card, they may play it.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A player cannot target themselves with offensive action cards, such asLucky Shot.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If an action card targets “any number”, “up to”, or “each” of a particular type of object, that action card may target zero of those objects. As such, these cards may be played even if they would cause no effect.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If an action card targets a specific number of a particular type of object, that action card cannot be played if those objects do not currently exist. For example,Repeal Lawcannot be played if there are no laws in play.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If a player has more than seven action cards, they must discard the excess immediately. They cannot play them to get down to seven, and the Hacan player cannot trade them.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: For notes about specific action cards, see theaction card component notes page.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Abilities
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Action Cards
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Status Phase
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: Move is an attribute of some units that is presented on faction sheets and unit upgrade technology cards.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A unit’s move value indicates the distance from its current system that it can move during theMovementstep of a tactical action.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: When an effect moves a unit to an adjacent system, modifying that unit’s move value will have no effect.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Modifiers
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Movement
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Ships
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Tactical Action
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Move (Attribute)
--- SECTION_ID: Related Topics
--- CONTENT: Units
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Survival Instinct
--- CONTENT: If the moved ships were in a gravity rift, they must roll for removal.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Miniaturization
--- CONTENT: Structures will be placed at the end of the tactical action. This will be after the production step, and so any space docks placed cannot use theirProductionability during the same action.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nano–Link Permit(Promissory Note)
--- CONTENT: The moved structures may use their unit abilities during the tactical action that they are moved.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nano–Link Permit(Promissory Note)
--- CONTENT: The structures are moved directly to the planet; they are not transported.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nanomachines(Technology)
--- CONTENT: When the Ral Nel player exhaustsNanomachines, they perform only one of the three component actions listed on the card.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nanomachines(Technology)
--- CONTENT: If the Ral Nel player has no PDS in their reinforcements when performing the first ability, they may remove one from a system that does not contain one of their command tokens to place it on a planet they control.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nanomachines(Technology)
--- CONTENT: The Ral Nel player may perform the second ability even if they have no damaged units, or even if they have no units with theSustain Damageability on the game board.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nanomachines(Technology)
--- CONTENT: The Ral Nel player must have at least one action card in their hand to perform the third ability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Nanomachines(Technology)
--- CONTENT: When performing the third ability, the Ral Nel player chooses which card they will discard before seeing which card they will draw.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Last Dispatch(Flagship)
--- CONTENT: A unit withSustain Damagecannot be destroyed, even if it is damaged.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Last Dispatch(Flagship)
--- CONTENT: If the Ral Nel player plays theSkilled Retreataction card, they cannot resolve the ability of theLast Dispatch.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Kan Kip Rel(Agent)
--- CONTENT: The action card that the Ral Nel player gives to another player must be one of the two that they drew, and not another action card from their hand.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Kan Kip Rel(Agent)
--- CONTENT: If the Yssaril player duplicates the effect of Kan Kip Rel with Ssruu, their agent, they will triggerScheming. They will draw three action cards, and give one of those three to another player. They will then add the remaining two to their hand, and then discard any action card from their hand.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Watchful Ojz(Commander)
--- CONTENT: If the Ral Nel player moves all their remaining ships, the combat ends immediately.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Watchful Ojz(Commander)
--- CONTENT: The Ral Nel player may transport fighters and ground forces if they move a ship with capacity.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Watchful Ojz(Commander)
--- CONTENT: The destination system may contain a planet controlled by another player, which may also have that player’s ground forces on it.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Watchful Ojz(Commander)
--- CONTENT: If the active system is a gravity rift, the moved ships must roll for removal.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Director Nel — Signal Intrusion(Hero)
--- CONTENT: Signal Intrusionmay be triggered by the Ral Nel player themself passing.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Director Nel — Signal Intrusion(Hero)
--- CONTENT: The Ral Nel player may take any number of turns after unpassing, before they pass again, which will end the action phase.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Director Nel — Signal Intrusion(Hero)
--- CONTENT: When the Ral Nel player passes again, they may score theProve Endurancesecret objective.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Data Skimmer(Breakthrough)
--- CONTENT: Action cards discarded by the Ral Nel player are placed in the action card discard pile, and not onData Skimmer.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Data Skimmer(Breakthrough)
--- CONTENT: An action card will be placed onData Skimmerif it is discarded after being played or cancelled, if it is discarded due to hand size limits, or if it is discarded for another game effect.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: The Ral Nel Consortium
--- SECTION_ID: Data Skimmer(Breakthrough)
--- CONTENT: Action cards onData Skimmerare not in the discard pile. They cannot be retrieved by abilities such as that ofThe Codexrelic.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: During theProductionstep of a tactical action, the active player can resolve theProductionability of each of their units that are in the active system to produce units
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: A unit’sProductionability, which is presented on a faction sheet or unit upgrade technology card, is always followed by a value. This value is the maximum number of units that this unit can produce.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When a player produces ships by usingProductionthat player must place them in the active system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: When a player produces ground forces, that player must place those units on planets that contain a unit that used itsProductionability.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Rules Reference
--- CONTENT: If a player uses theProductionability of a unit in a space area of a system to produce ground forces, those ground forces may either be placed on a planet the player controls in that system or in the space area of that system.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: A unit’sProductionvalue is the maximum number of units that may be produced by that unit, regardless of cost. For example, a space dock with “Production6” could produce six dreadnoughts or six fighters.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: Placement of produced units is not limited by a unit’sProductionvalue, only by the location of the producing units.
##################################################

### RULE_SOURCE: Production (Unit Ability)
--- SECTION_ID: Notes
--- CONTENT: If an effect allows a player to produce a ship of a specific type, then factional variations do not prevent that player from producing that type of ship.
##################################################
